			/* decrypt helper function */
		function decryptCharcode(n,start,end,offset) {
			n = n + offset;
			if (offset > 0 && n > end) {
				n = start + (n - end - 1);
			} else if (offset < 0 && n < start) {
				n = end - (start - n - 1);
			}
			return String.fromCharCode(n);
		}
			/* decrypt string */
		function decryptString(enc,offset) {
			var dec = "";
			var len = enc.length;
			for(var i=0; i < len; i++) {
				var n = enc.charCodeAt(i);
				if (n >= 0x2B && n <= 0x3A) {
					dec += decryptCharcode(n,0x2B,0x3A,offset);	/* 0-9 . , - + / : */
				} else if (n >= 0x40 && n <= 0x5A) {
					dec += decryptCharcode(n,0x40,0x5A,offset);	/* A-Z @ */
				} else if (n >= 0x61 && n <= 0x7A) {
					dec += decryptCharcode(n,0x61,0x7A,offset);	/* a-z */
				} else {
					dec += enc.charAt(i);
				}
			}
			return dec;
		}
			/* decrypt spam-protected emails */
		function linkTo_UnCryptMailto(s) {
			location.href = decryptString(s,7);
		}

group</strong></h1><h3 class="align-center">Sophisticated threat actor, linked to previous ‘<strong>BlackEnergy</strong>’ cyberattacks, targets high-value organizations</h3></div></div></div></div></div><!--TYPO3SEARCH_begin--><div id="main-content"><div id="content-1747306" class="section faded-opaque skin-default skin-padding-bottom-small "><div skin-mb-l skin-mt-l"><div class="col col-sm-6 "><div id="content-c1747668" class="frame frame-default frame-type-text frame-layout-0"><header><h3 class="bigger "> GreyEnergy finally exposed </h3></header><p>ESET researchers just <a href="https://www.welivesecurity.com/2018/10/17/greyenergy-updated-arsenal-dangerous-threat-actors/" title="welivesecurity" target="_blank">unmasked the shadowy cyber-espionage group</a> dubbed GreyEnergy. It’s the successor to the BlackEnergy APT group which went ‘underground‘ a few years ago after terrorizing Ukraine until 2015. It’s also closely related to TeleBots, responsible for NotPetya, perhaps the most damaging cyberattack experienced. </p><p>Our researchers have demonstrated beyond doubt that GreyEnergy’s malware toolkit both <strong>mirrors and improves on already-sophisticated techniques</strong> used in the devastating NotPetya attacks and Ukraine power grid outages. </p></div></div><div class="col col-sm-6 "><div id="content-c1747666" class="frame frame-default frame-type-text frame-layout-0"><blockquote><p>ESET’s exposure of GreyEnergy is important for a successful defense against this particular threat actor as well as for better understanding the tactics, tools and procedures of the most advanced APT groups.</p></blockquote><p class="align-right">Anton Cherepanov, ESET Senior Malware Researcher</p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div id="content-1747754" class="section faded-opaque skin-default "><span class="rimg section-image hidden" data-remote=".section" class="frame frame-default frame-type-text frame-layout-0 skin-mb-medium skin-padding-m"><header><h3 class="bigger align-center"> Organizations at risk </h3></header></div><div id="content-c1747268" class="csc-frame csc-frame-default"><div class="row flex skin-gutter-l skin-padding-m skin-mb-s"><div class="col col-sm-6 "><div id="content-c1747289" class="frame frame-default frame-type-text frame-layout-0"><p>The consequences for organizations of all sizes can be devastating. Compared to BlackEnergy, GreyEnergy is a more modern toolkit with an even <strong>greater focus on stealth</strong>. ESET researchers have demonstrated that GreyEnergy has the capacity to<strong> take full control of entire company networks.</strong></p><p>One basic stealth technique is to push only selected modules to selected targets, and only when needed. In addition, some GreyEnergy modules are partially encrypted and some remain fileless – running only in memory – with the intention of hindering analysis and detection.</p></div></div><div class="col col-sm-6 "><div id="content-c1747609" class="frame frame-default frame-type-text frame-layout-0"><p>To cover their tracks, typically, GreyEnergy’s operators securely wipe the malware components from the victims’ hard drives. </p><p>The modules described in ESET’s analysis were used for <strong>espionage and reconnaissance</strong> purposes and include: backdoor, file extraction, taking screenshots, keylogging, password and credential stealing.</p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div id="content-1747296" class="section faded-opaque skin-default "><div class="container" ><div class="section-content"><div id="content-c1747291" class="frame frame-default frame-type-text frame-layout-0 skin-mb-medium skin-padding-m"><header><h3 class="bigger align-center"> How ESET protects you </h3></header><p class="align-center">The good news is ESET can fully protect your organization. Our multilayered technology<strong></strong>combining machine learning, human expertise and global threat intelligence, <strong>combats exactly this type of new, previously unseen threat</strong>. </p></div><div id="content-c1747743" class="csc-frame csc-frame-default"><div class="row flex hidden-to-md skin-mb-l"><div class="col col-sm-4 "><div id="content-c1747744" class="frame frame-default frame-type-text frame-layout-0"><header><h4 class="bold"> ESET Enterprise Inspector </h4></header><p> Is the most flexible and custom-fit EDR solution on the market. It evaluates behavior of all submitted samples with threat intelligence feeds, ESET’s multiple internal tools for static and dynamic analysis and reputation data to detect zero-day threats.</p></div></div><div class="col col-sm-4 "><div id="content-c1747746" class="frame frame-default frame-type-text frame-layout-0"><header><h4 class="bold"> ESET Mail Security </h4></header><p>ESET Mail Security award-winning solutions provide powerful server malware protection, spam filtering, anti-phishing and thorough email scanning against all email-borne threats.
